Fountain in Moscow's <a href="/wiki/Square_of_Europe" title="Square of Europe">Square of Europe</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tverskaya_Street_in_Moscow_by_night_(no_cars).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Tverskaya_Street_in_Moscow_by_night_%28no_cars%29.JPG/220px-Tverskaya_Street_in_Moscow_by_night_%28no_cars%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Tverskaya_Street_in_Moscow_by_night_%28no_cars%29.JPG/330px-Tverskaya_Street_in_Moscow_by_night_%28no_cars%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Tverskaya_Street_in_Moscow_by_night_%28no_cars%29.JPG/440px-Tverskaya_Street_in_Moscow_by_night_%28no_cars%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tverskaya_Street_in_Moscow_by_night_(no_cars).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Tverskaya_Street" title="Tverskaya Street">Tverskaya Street</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city is full of clubs, restaurants and bars. <a href="/wiki/Tverskaya_Street" title="Tverskaya Street">Tverskaya Street</a> is also one of the busiest shopping streets in Moscow.</p>
<p>The adjoining <a href="/wiki/Tretyakovsky_Proyezd" title="Tretyakovsky Proyezd">Tretyakovsky Proyezd</a>, also south of Tverskaya Street, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kitai-gorod" title="Kitai-gorod">Kitai-gorod</a>, is host to upmarket boutique stores such as <a href="/wiki/Bulgari" title="Bulgari">Bulgari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tiffany_%26_Co." title="Tiffany &amp; Co.">Tiffany &amp; Co.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armani" title="Armani">Armani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prada" title="Prada">Prada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bentley" title="Bentley">Bentley</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-go-mag_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-go-mag-104">[104]</a></sup> Nightlife in Moscow has moved on since Soviet times and today the city has many of the world's largest nightclubs. Clubs, bars, creative spaces and restaurants-turned-into-dancefloors are flooding Moscow streets with new openings every year. The hottest area is located around the old chocolate factory, where bars, nightclubs, galleries, cafés and restaurants are placed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moscow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Presnya.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="340" data-file-width="442" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Presnya.JPG/220px-Presnya.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Presnya.JPG/330px-Presnya.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Presnya.JPG/440px-Presnya.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Presnya.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View from the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Sisters_(Moscow)" title="Seven Sisters (Moscow)">Seven Sisters</a> in Kudrinskaya Square. The mayor's highrise office (the former <a href="/wiki/Comecon" title="Comecon">Comecon</a> headquarters) is to the left, the Russian government building to the right</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_Russia-2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2133" data-file-width="2231" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_Russia-2.jpg/220px-Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_Russia-2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_Russia-2.jpg/330px-Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_Russia-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_Russia-2.jpg/440px-Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_Russia-2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_Russia-2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_of_Russia_main_building" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs of Russia main building">Ministry of Foreign Affairs of Russia main building</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Krasnopresnenskaya_2_01.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1200" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Krasnopresnenskaya_2_01.JPG/220px-Krasnopresnenskaya_2_01.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Krasnopresnenskaya_2_01.JPG/330px-Krasnopresnenskaya_2_01.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Krasnopresnenskaya_2_01.JPG/440px-Krasnopresnenskaya_2_01.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Krasnopresnenskaya_2_01.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/White_House_(Moscow)" title="White House (Moscow)">White House</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Moscow is the seat of power for the Russian Federation. At the centre of the city, in the <a href="/wiki/Central_Administrative_Okrug" title="Central Administrative Okrug">Central Administrative Okrug</a>, is the Moscow Kremlin, which houses the home of the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Russia" title="President of Russia">President of Russia</a> as well as national governmental facilities. This includes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_the_Russian_Federation" title="Armed Forces of the Russian Federation">military headquarters</a> and the headquarters of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Federal_Security_Service_(Russia)" title="Federal Security Service (Russia)">Federal Security Service</a>. Moscow, like with any national <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capital_(political)" title="Capital (political)">capital</a>, is also the host of all the foreign <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_in_Russia" title="List of diplomatic missions in Russia">embassies</a> and diplomats <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Russia" title="Foreign relations of Russia">representing a multitude of nations in Russia</a>.</p>
<p>Moscow is designated as one of three <a href="/wiki/Federal_cities_of_Russia" title="Federal cities of Russia">federal cities of Russia</a> – the others being <a href="/wiki/Saint_Petersburg" title="Saint Petersburg">Saint Petersburg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sevastopol" title="Sevastopol">Sevastopol</a> (although the status of the latter is <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Crimea" title="Political status of Crimea">disputed</a>). Among the 85 <a href="/wiki/Federal_subjects_of_Russia" title="Federal subjects of Russia">federal subjects of Russia</a>, Moscow represents the most populated one and the second-smallest one in terms of area. Moscow is located within the <a href="/wiki/Central_economic_region" title="Central economic region">central economic region</a>, one of <a href="/wiki/Economic_regions_of_Russia" title="Economic regions of Russia">twelve regions</a> within Russia with similar economic goals. The <a href="/wiki/Basic_law" title="Basic law">basic law</a> of the city is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charter_of_Moscow" title="Charter of Moscow">Charter of Moscow</a> that was adopted in 1995.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Executive">Executive</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moscow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Executive">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Moscow" title="Mayor of Moscow">Mayor of Moscow</a> is the leading official in the executive, leading the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Moscow" title="Government of Moscow">Government of Moscow</a> which is the highest organ of executive power.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Moscow_City_Duma">Moscow City Duma</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moscow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Moscow City Duma">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Moscow_City_Duma" title="Moscow City Duma">Moscow City Duma</a></div>
<p>The Moscow City Duma is the <a href="/wiki/City_Duma" title="City Duma">City Duma</a> (<a href="/wiki/City_council" title="City council">city council</a> or local <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">parliament</a>) and local laws must be approved by it. It includes 35 members who are elected for a four-year term in a <a href="/wiki/Mixed-member_proportional_representation" title="Mixed-member proportional representation">Mixed-member proportional representation</a>: 18 are elected on a <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional party list</a> basis and 17 on <a href="/wiki/Electoral_district" title="Electoral district">Single-mandate constituency</a> basis.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moscow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Msk_all_districts.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6437" data-file-width="4842" height="292" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Msk_all_districts.svg/220px-Msk_all_districts.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Msk_all_districts.svg/330px-Msk_all_districts.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Msk_all_districts.svg/440px-Msk_all_districts.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Msk_all_districts.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Moscow" title="Administrative divisions of Moscow">Administrative okrugs of Moscow</a>: 1. Central 2. Northern 3. North-Eastern 4. Eastern 5. South-Eastern 6. Southern 7. South-Western 8. Western 9. North-Western 10. Zelenogradsky 11. Novomoskovsky 12. Troitsky</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Moscow" title="Administrative divisions of Moscow">Administrative divisions of Moscow</a></div>
<p>The entire city of Moscow is headed by one mayor (<a href="/wiki/Sergey_Sobyanin" title="Sergey Sobyanin">Sergey Sobyanin</a>). The city of Moscow is divided into twelve administrative okrugs and 123 districts.</p>
<p>The Russian capital's town-planning development began to show as early as the 12th century, when the city was founded. The central part of Moscow grew by consolidating with suburbs in line with medieval principles of urban development, when strong fortress walls would gradually spread along the circle streets of adjacent new settlements. The first circular defence walls set the trajectory of Moscow's rings, laying the groundwork for the future planning of the Russian capital.</p>
<p>The following fortifications served as the city's circular defense boundaries at some point in history: the Kremlin walls, Zemlyanoy Gorod (Earthwork Town), the Kamer-Kollezhsky Rampart, the Garden Ring, and the small railway ring. The Moscow Automobile Ring Road (MKAD) has been Moscow's boundary since 1960. Also in the form of a circle are the main Moscow subway line, the Ring Line, and the so-called Third Automobile Ring, which was completed in 2005. Hence, the characteristic radial-circle planning continues to define Moscow's further development. However, contemporary Moscow has also engulfed a number of territories outside the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Ring_Road" title="Moscow Ring Road">Ring Road</a>, such as Solntsevo, Butovo, and the town of <a href="/wiki/Zelenograd" title="Zelenograd">Zelenograd</a>. A part of <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Oblast" title="Moscow Oblast">Moscow Oblast</a>'s territory was merged into Moscow on July 1, 2012; as a result, Moscow is no longer fully surrounded by Moscow Oblast and now also has a border with <a href="/wiki/Kaluga_Oblast" title="Kaluga Oblast">Kaluga Oblast</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Merger_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-Merger-106">[106]</a></sup> In all, Moscow gained about 1,500 square kilometers (580 sq mi) and 230,000 inhabitants. Moscow's Mayor Sergey Sobyanin lauded the expansion that will help Moscow and the neighboring region, a "mega-city" of twenty million people, to develop "harmonically".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Merger2_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Merger2-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>All administrative okrugs and districts have their own <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coats of arms</a> and flags as well as individual heads of the area.</p>
<p>In addition to the districts, there are Territorial Units with Special Status. These usually include areas with small or no permanent populations. Such is the case with the All-Russia Exhibition Centre, the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Botanical_Garden_of_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Moscow Botanical Garden of Academy of Sciences">Botanical Garden</a>, large parks, and industrial zones. In recent years, some territories have been merged with different districts. There are no ethnic-specific regions in Moscow, as in the <a href="/wiki/Chinatown" title="Chinatown">Chinatowns</a> that exist in some <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North American</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">East Asian</a> cities. And although districts are not designated by income, as with most cities, those areas that are closer to the city center, metro stations or green zones are considered more prestigious.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>Moscow also hosts some of the government bodies of <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Oblast" title="Moscow Oblast">Moscow Oblast</a>, although the city itself is not a part of the oblast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MoscowO_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-MoscowO-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moscow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Russia" title="Economy of Russia">Economy of Russia</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview_2">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moscow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moscow-City2015.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="683" data-file-width="1024" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Moscow-City2015.jpg/220px-Moscow-City2015.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Moscow-City2015.jpg/330px-Moscow-City2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Moscow-City2015.jpg/440px-Moscow-City2015.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moscow-City2015.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Moscow_International_Business_Center" title="Moscow International Business Center">MIBC</a>, one of the largest financial centres in Europe</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Moscow has one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_by_GDP" title="List of cities by GDP">largest municipal economies in Europe</a> and it accounts more than 1/5 of Russian GDP.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Moscow&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the Nominal <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/GRP" title="GRP">GRP</a> in Moscow reached 12 trillion roubles<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> (USD 0.31 trillion) and USD 30,000 per capita.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>Moscow has the lowest unemployment rate of all <a href="/wiki/Federal_subjects_of_Russia" title="Federal subjects of Russia">federal subjects of Russia</a>, standing at just 1% in 2010, compared to the national average of 7%. The average monthly wage in the city is 60,000 roubles (about 2000 USD), which is almost twice the national average of 27,000 rubles (900 USD), and the highest among the federal subjects of Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bofit_42_2010_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-bofit_42_2010-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<p>Moscow is the financial center of Russia and home to the country's largest banks and many of its largest companies, such as natural gas giant <a href="/wiki/Gazprom" title="Gazprom">Gazprom</a>. Moscow accounts for 17% of retail sales in Russia and for 13% of all construction activity in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bofit_42_2010_112-1"><a href="#cite_note-bofit_42_2010-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Since the <a href="/wiki/1998_Russian_financial_crisis" title="1998 Russian financial crisis">1998 Russian financial crisis</a>, business sectors in Moscow have shown exponential rates of growth. Many new business centers and office buildings have been built in recent years, but Moscow still experiences shortages in office space. As a result, many former industrial and research facilities are being reconstructed to become suitable for office use. Overall, economic stability has improved in recent years; nonetheless, crime and corruption continue still hinder business development.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:World_Trade_Centre_in_Moscow.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="638" data-file-width="1111" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/World_Trade_Centre_in_Moscow.jpg/220px-World_Trade_Centre_in_Moscow.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/World_Trade_Centre_in_Moscow.jpg/330px-World_Trade_Centre_in_Moscow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/World_Trade_Centre_in_Moscow.jpg/440px-World_Trade_Centre_in_Moscow.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:World_Trade_Centre_in_Moscow.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
World Trade Center in Moscow</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Cherkizovskiy marketplace was the largest marketplace in Europe, with a daily turnover of about thirty million dollars and about ten thousand venders<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> from different countries (including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="People's Republic of China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> and <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>). It was administratively divided into twelve parts and covers a wide sector of the city. Since July 2009 it has been closed.</p>
<p>In 2008, Moscow had 74 billionaires with an average wealth of $5.9 billion, which placed it above New York's 71 billionaires. However, as of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Moscow&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 27 billionaires in Moscow compared with New York's 55 billionaires. Overall, Russia <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Russian_billionaires_by_net_worth" title="List of Russian billionaires by net worth">lost 52 billionaires</a> during the recession.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> Topping the list of Russia's billionaires in 2009 is <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Prokhorov" title="Mikhail Prokhorov">Mikhail Prokhorov</a> with $9.5 billion, ahead of the more famous <a href="/wiki/Roman_Abramovich" title="Roman Abramovich">Roman Abramovich</a> with $8.5 billion, in <a class="extiw" href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%BA_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B9%D1%88%D0%B8%D1%85_%D0%B1%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2_%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B8_(2009)" title="ru:Список богатейших бизнесменов России (2009)">2nd place</a>. Prokhorov's holding company, "ОНЭКСИМ" (<i>ONÈKSIM</i>) group, owns huge assets in hydrogen energy, nanotechnology, traditional energy, precious metals sector, while Abramovich, since selling his oil company Sibneft to Russian state-controlled gas giant Gazprom in 2005, has bought up steel and mining assets. He also owns <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea F.C.</a>. Russia's richest woman remains <a href="/wiki/Yelena_Baturina" title="Yelena Baturina">Yelena Baturina</a>, the 50-year-old second wife of Moscow Mayor Yuri Luzhkov. <a href="/wiki/Oleg_Deripaska" title="Oleg Deripaska">Oleg Deripaska</a>, the 1st on this list in 2008 with $28 billion, was only 10th in 2009 with <a class="extiw" href="https://ru.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%81%D0%BE%D0%BA_%D0%B1%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B9%D1%88%D0%B8%D1%85_%D0%B1%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%BD%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B2_%D0%A0%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%B8_(2009)" title="ru:Список богатейших бизнесменов России (2009)">$3.5 billion</a>. Based on <a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a>' 2011 list of the world's billionaires, Moscow is the city with the most billionaires in the world, with 79 from 115 in all of Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Nouveau_riche" title="Nouveau riche">nouveau riche</a>, also called the "New Russians", often in a derogatory sense, have a reputation for flaunting their wealth; the avenues for doing so have also increased in recent times at the many <a href="/wiki/Haute_couture" title="Haute couture">haute couture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Haute_cuisine" title="Haute cuisine">haute cuisine</a> spots in Moscow.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry">Industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moscow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Primary <a href="/wiki/Industry" title="Industry">industries</a> in Moscow include the <a href="/wiki/Chemical_industry" title="Chemical industry">chemical</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metallurgy" title="Metallurgy">metallurgy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Food_industry" title="Food industry">food</a>, <a href="/wiki/Textile" title="Textile">textile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Furniture" title="Furniture">furniture</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Energy_production" title="Energy production">energy production</a>, <a href="/wiki/Software_development" title="Software development">software development</a> and <a href="/wiki/Machine" title="Machine">machinery</a> industries.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Superjet_100_first_display.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="850" data-file-width="1198" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Superjet_100_first_display.jpg/220px-Superjet_100_first_display.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Superjet_100_first_display.jpg/330px-Superjet_100_first_display.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Superjet_100_first_display.jpg/440px-Superjet_100_first_display.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Superjet_100_first_display.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OKB_Sukhoi" title="OKB Sukhoi">OKB Sukhoi</a> aircraft design bureau is based in Moscow</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Mil_Moscow_Helicopter_Plant" title="Mil Moscow Helicopter Plant">Mil Moscow Helicopter Plant</a> is one of the leading producers of military and civil helicopters in the world. <a href="/wiki/Khrunichev_State_Research_and_Production_Space_Center" title="Khrunichev State Research and Production Space Center">Khrunichev State Research and Production Space Center</a> produces various space equipment, including modules for space stations <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">Mir</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salyut" title="Salyut">Salyut</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISS" title="ISS">ISS</a> as well as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proton_(rocket)" title="Proton (rocket)">Proton launch vehicles</a> and military <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ICBM" title="ICBM">ICBMs</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sukhoi" title="Sukhoi">Sukhoi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ilyushin" title="Ilyushin">Ilyushin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mikoyan" title="Mikoyan">Mikoyan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tupolev" title="Tupolev">Tupolev</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yakovlev" title="Yakovlev">Yakovlev</a> aircraft design bureaus also situated in Moscow. <a href="/wiki/NPO_Energomash" title="NPO Energomash">NPO Energomash</a>, producing the <a href="/wiki/Rocket_engine" title="Rocket engine">rocket engines</a> for Russian and American space programs, as well as <a href="/wiki/Lavochkin" title="Lavochkin">Lavochkin</a> design bureau, which built <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fighter_plane" title="Fighter plane">fighter planes</a> during WWII, but switched to <a href="/wiki/Space_probe" title="Space probe">space probes</a> since the <a href="/wiki/Space_Race" title="Space Race">Space Race</a>, are in nearby <a href="/wiki/Khimki" title="Khimki">Khimki</a>, an independent city in <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Oblast" title="Moscow Oblast">Moscow Oblast</a> that have largely been enclosed by Moscow from its sides. Automobile plants <a href="/wiki/ZiL" title="ZiL">ZiL</a> and <a href="/wiki/AZLK" title="AZLK">AZLK</a>, as well as the Voitovich Rail Vehicle plant, are situated in Moscow and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metrovagonmash" title="Metrovagonmash">Metrovagonmash</a> metro wagon plant is located just outside the city limits. The <a href="/wiki/Poljot" title="Poljot">Poljot Moscow watch factory</a> produces military, professional and sport watches well known in Russia and abroad. <a href="/wiki/Yuri_Gagarin" title="Yuri Gagarin">Yuri Gagarin</a> in his trip into space used "Shturmanskie" produced by this factory.</p>
<p>The Electrozavod factory was the first transformer factory in Russia. The Kristall distillery<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> is the oldest distillery in Russia producing <a href="/wiki/Vodka" title="Vodka">vodka</a> types, including "<a href="/wiki/Stolichnaya" title="Stolichnaya">Stolichnaya</a>" while wines are produced at Moscow wine plants, including the Moscow Interrepublican Vinery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> The Moscow Jewelry Factory<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> and the Jewellerprom<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> are producers of jewellery in Russia; Jewellerprom used to produce the exclusive <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Victory" title="Order of Victory">Order of Victory</a>, awarded to those aiding the Soviet Union's Red Army during World War II.</p>
<p>There are other industries located just outside the city of Moscow, as well as microelectronic industries in Zelenograd, including <a href="/wiki/Ruselectronics" title="Ruselectronics">Ruselectronics</a> companies.</p>
<p>Gazprom, the largest extractor of <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> in the world and the largest <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Russia" title="Economy of Russia">Russian company</a>, has head offices also in Moscow, as well as other oil, gas and electricity companies.</p>
<p>Moscow hosts headquarters of the many of <a href="/wiki/Telecommunication" title="Telecommunication">telecommunication</a> and <a href="/wiki/Technology_company" title="Technology company">technology</a> companies, including <a href="/wiki/1C_Company" title="1C Company">1C</a>, <a href="/wiki/ABBYY" title="ABBYY">ABBYY</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beeline_(brand)" title="Beeline (brand)">Beeline</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kaspersky_Lab" title="Kaspersky Lab">Kaspersky Lab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mail.Ru" title="Mail.Ru">Mail.Ru Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/MegaFon" title="MegaFon">MegaFon</a>, <a href="/wiki/MTS_(network_provider)" title="MTS (network provider)">MTS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rambler_(portal)" title="Rambler (portal)">Rambler&amp;Co</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rostelecom" title="Rostelecom">Rostelecom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yandex" title="Yandex">Yandex</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yota" title="Yota">Yota</a>.</p>
<p>Some industry is being transferred out of the city to improve the ecological state of the city.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Living_costs">Living costs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moscow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Living costs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Triumph_Palace.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="380" data-file-width="524" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Triumph_Palace.jpg/250px-Triumph_Palace.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Triumph_Palace.jpg/375px-Triumph_Palace.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Triumph_Palace.jpg/500px-Triumph_Palace.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Triumph_Palace.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Triumph_Palace" title="Triumph Palace">Triumph Palace</a>, tallest apartment building in Europe.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a> times, apartments were lent to people by the government according to the square meters-per-person norm (some groups, including people's artists, heroes and prominent scientists had bonuses according to their honors). <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Private_ownership" title="Private ownership">Private ownership</a> of apartments was limited until the 1990s, when people were permitted to secure property rights to the places they inhabited. Since the Soviet era, estate owners have had to pay the service charge for their residences, a fixed amount based on persons per living area.</p>
<p>The price of <a href="/wiki/Real_estate" title="Real estate">real estate</a> in Moscow continues to rise. Today, one could expect to pay $4000 on average per square meter (11 sq ft) on the outskirts of the city<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> or US$6,500–$8,000 per square meter in a prestigious district. The price sometimes may exceed US$40,000 per square meter in a flat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> It costs about US$1200 per month to rent a 1-bedroom apartment and about US$1000 per month for a studio in the center of Moscow.</p>
<p>A typical one-bedroom apartment is about thirty square metres (320 <a href="/wiki/Square_foot" title="Square foot">square feet</a>), a typical two-bedroom apartment is forty-five square metres (480 square feet), and a typical three-bedroom apartment is seventy square metres (750 square feet). Many cannot move out of their apartments, especially if a family lives in a two-room apartment originally granted by the state during the Soviet era. Some city residents have attempted to cope with the cost of living by renting their apartments while staying in <a href="/wiki/Dacha" title="Dacha">dachas</a> (country houses) outside the city.</p>
<p>In 2006, Mercer Human Resources Consulting named Moscow the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_most_expensive_cities_for_expatriate_employees" title="List of most expensive cities for expatriate employees">most expensive city for expatriate employees</a>, ahead of perennial winner Tokyo, due to the stable <a href="/wiki/Russian_ruble" title="Russian ruble">Russian ruble</a> as well as increasing housing prices within the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> Moscow also ranked first in the 2007 edition and 2008 edition of the survey. However, Tokyo has overtaken Moscow as the most expensive city in the world, placing Moscow at third and behind Osaka at second.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mercer.com_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-mercer.com-126">[126]</a></sup> Critics of their methodology argue that this survey replicates the lifestyle that a senior executive would have in Washington DC, counting certain very expensive brand name foreign goods, but disregarding the many lines that are far cheaper in Russia, e.g. household staff, drivers, nannies, etc.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In 2008, Moscow ranked top on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_most_expensive_cities" title="List of most expensive cities">list of most expensive cities</a> for the third year in a row.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, according to Forbes, Moscow ranked the 9th most expensive city in the world. Forbes ranked Moscow the 2nd most expensive city the year prior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_education">Science and education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moscow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Science and education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Russia" title="Education in Russia">Education in Russia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Golden_brain.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1029" data-file-width="1375" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Golden_brain.png/220px-Golden_brain.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Golden_brain.png/330px-Golden_brain.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Golden_brain.png/440px-Golden_brain.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Golden_brain.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Russian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Russian Academy of Sciences">Russian Academy of Sciences</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There are 1696 high schools in Moscow, as well as 91 colleges.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mosru-stats_79-2"><a href="#cite_note-mosru-stats-79">[79]</a></sup> Besides these, there are 222 institutions of higher education, including 60 state universities<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mosru-stats_79-3"><a href="#cite_note-mosru-stats-79">[79]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_State_University" title="Moscow State University">Lomonosov Moscow State University</a>, which was founded in 1755.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-msu-history_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-msu-history-129">[129]</a></sup> The main university building located in Vorobyovy Gory (<a href="/wiki/Sparrow_Hills" title="Sparrow Hills">Sparrow Hills</a>) is 240 metres (790 ft) tall and when completed, was the tallest building on the continent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> The university has over 30,000 <a href="/wiki/Undergraduate_education" title="Undergraduate education">undergraduate</a> and 7,000 <a href="/wiki/Postgraduate_education" title="Postgraduate education">postgraduate</a> students, who have a choice of twenty-nine faculties and 450 departments for study. Additionally, approximately 10,000 high school students take courses at the university, while over two thousand researchers work. The Moscow State University library contains over nine million books, making it one of the largest libraries in all of Russia. Its acclaim throughout the international academic community has meant that over 11,000 international students have graduated from the university, with many coming to Moscow to learn the <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian language</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/I.M._Sechenov_First_Moscow_State_Medical_University" title="I.M. Sechenov First Moscow State Medical University">I.M. Sechenov First Moscow State Medical University</a> named after <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Sechenov" title="Ivan Sechenov">Ivan Sechenov</a> or formerly known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moscow_Medical_Academy" title="Moscow Medical Academy">Moscow Medical Academy</a> (<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=1stMSMU&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="1stMSMU (page does not exist)">1stMSMU</a>) is a medical university situated in Moscow, Russia. It was founded in 1785 as the faculty of the Moscow state University. It is a Russian Federal Agency for Health and Social Development. It is one of the largest medical universities in Russia and Europe. More than 9200 students are enrolled in 115 academic departments. It offers courses for post-graduate studies.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2016-MSU.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1187" data-file-width="2050" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/2016-MSU.jpg/220px-2016-MSU.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/2016-MSU.jpg/330px-2016-MSU.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/2016-MSU.jpg/440px-2016-MSU.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2016-MSU.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Moscow_State_University" title="Moscow State University">Moscow State University</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Moscow is one of the financial centers of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Federation" title="Russian Federation">Russian Federation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Independent_States" title="Commonwealth of Independent States">CIS</a> countries and is known for its business schools. Among them are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Finance_Academy_under_the_Government_of_RF" title="Finance Academy under the Government of RF">Finance Academy under the Government of RF</a>; <a href="/wiki/Plekhanov_Russian_University_of_Economics" title="Plekhanov Russian University of Economics">Plekhanov Russian University of Economics</a>; <a href="/wiki/The_State_University_of_Management" title="The State University of Management">The State University of Management</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_University_-_Higher_School_of_Economics" title="State University - Higher School of Economics">State University - Higher School of Economics</a>. They offer undergraduate degrees in management, finance, accounting, marketing, real estate and economic theory, as well as Masters programs and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MBA" title="MBA">MBAs</a>.Most of them have branches in other regions of Russia and countries around the world.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%97%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B81.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3216" data-file-width="4288" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/%D0%97%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B81.jpg/220px-%D0%97%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B81.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/%D0%97%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B81.jpg/330px-%D0%97%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B81.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/%D0%97%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B81.jpg/440px-%D0%97%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B81.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%97%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B2%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%B81.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Entrance to the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Conservatory" title="Moscow Conservatory">Moscow Conservatory</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bauman_Moscow_State_Technical_University" title="Bauman Moscow State Technical University">Bauman Moscow State Technical University</a>, founded in 1830, is located in the center of Moscow and provides 18,000 undergraduate and 1,000 postgraduate students with an education in science and engineering, offering technical degrees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> Since it opened enrollment to students from outside of Russia in 1991, Bauman Moscow State Technical University has increased its number of international students up to two hundred.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Conservatory" title="Moscow Conservatory">Moscow Conservatory</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> founded in 1866 is a prominent music school in Russia, whose graduates include <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Rachmaninoff" title="Sergei Rachmaninoff">Sergey Rachmaninoff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Scriabin" title="Alexander Scriabin">Alexander Scriabin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aram_Khachaturian" title="Aram Khachaturian">Aram Khachaturian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mstislav_Rostropovich" title="Mstislav Rostropovich">Mstislav Rostropovich</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Schnittke" title="Alfred Schnittke">Alfred Schnittke</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Gerasimov_Institute_of_Cinematography" title="Gerasimov Institute of Cinematography">Gerasimov All-Russian State Institute of Cinematography</a>, abbreviated as VGIK, is the world's oldest educational institution in <a href="/wiki/Cinematography" title="Cinematography">Cinematography</a>, founded by <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Gardin" title="Vladimir Gardin">Vladimir Gardin</a> in 1919. <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Eisenstein" title="Sergei Eisenstein">Sergei Eisenstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vsevolod_Pudovkin" title="Vsevolod Pudovkin">Vsevolod Pudovkin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Aleksey_Batalov" title="Aleksey Batalov">Aleksey Batalov</a> were among its most distinguished professors and <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Vartanov" title="Mikhail Vartanov">Mikhail Vartanov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sergei_Parajanov" title="Sergei Parajanov">Sergei Parajanov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andrei_Tarkovsky" title="Andrei Tarkovsky">Andrei Tarkovsky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Mikhalkov" title="Nikita Mikhalkov">Nikita Mikhalkov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eldar_Ryazanov" title="Eldar Ryazanov">Eldar Ryazanov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Sokurov" title="Alexander Sokurov">Alexander Sokurov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yuriy_Norshteyn" title="Yuriy Norshteyn">Yuriy Norshteyn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aleksandr_Petrov_(animator)" title="Aleksandr Petrov (animator)">Aleksandr Petrov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vasily_Shukshin" title="Vasily Shukshin">Vasily Shukshin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Konrad_Wolf" title="Konrad Wolf">Konrad Wolf</a> among graduates.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mstu_iauza.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="454" data-file-width="604" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Mstu_iauza.jpg/220px-Mstu_iauza.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Mstu_iauza.jpg/330px-Mstu_iauza.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Mstu_iauza.jpg/440px-Mstu_iauza.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mstu_iauza.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bauman_Moscow_State_Technical_University" title="Bauman Moscow State Technical University">Bauman Moscow State Technical University</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vgik.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2188" data-file-width="2856" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Vgik.jpg/220px-Vgik.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Vgik.jpg/330px-Vgik.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Vgik.jpg/440px-Vgik.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vgik.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Gerasimov_Institute_of_Cinematography" title="Gerasimov Institute of Cinematography">Gerasimov Institute of Cinematography</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Moscow_State_Institute_of_International_Relations" title="Moscow State Institute of International Relations">Moscow State Institute of International Relations</a>, founded in 1944, remains Russia's best- known school of international relations and diplomacy, with six schools focused on international relations. Approximately 4,500 students make up the university's student body and over 700,000 Russian and foreign-language books — of which 20,000 are considered rare — can be found in the library of the Moscow State Institute of International Relations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other institutions are the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Institute_of_Physics_and_Technology" title="Moscow Institute of Physics and Technology">Moscow Institute of Physics and Technology</a>, also known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phystech" title="Phystech">Phystech</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Fyodorov_Eye_Microsurgery_Complex" title="Fyodorov Eye Microsurgery Complex">Fyodorov Eye Microsurgery Complex</a>, founded in 1988 by Russian eye surgeon <a href="/wiki/Svyatoslav_Fyodorov" title="Svyatoslav Fyodorov">Svyatoslav Fyodorov</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Aviation_Institute" title="Moscow Aviation Institute">Moscow Aviation Institute</a>, the Moscow Motorway Institute (State Technical University), and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moscow_Engineering_Physics_Institute" title="Moscow Engineering Physics Institute">Moscow Engineering Physics Institute</a>. <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Institute_of_Physics_and_Technology" title="Moscow Institute of Physics and Technology">Moscow Institute of Physics and Technology</a> has taught numerous <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a> winners, including <a href="/wiki/Pyotr_Kapitsa" title="Pyotr Kapitsa">Pyotr Kapitsa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nikolay_Semyonov" title="Nikolay Semyonov">Nikolay Semyonov</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lev_Landau" title="Lev Landau">Lev Landau</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Prokhorov" title="Alexander Prokhorov">Alexander Prokhorov</a>, while the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moscow_Engineering_Physics_Institute" title="Moscow Engineering Physics Institute">Moscow Engineering Physics Institute</a> is known for its research in <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_physics" title="Nuclear physics">nuclear physics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> The highest Russian military school is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frunze_Military_Academy" title="Frunze Military Academy">Combined Arms Academy of the Armed Forces of the Russian Federation</a>.</p>
<p>Although Moscow has a number of famous Soviet-era higher educational institutions, most of which are more oriented towards <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">engineering</a> or the fundamental sciences, in recent years Moscow has seen a growth in the number of commercial and private institutions that offer classes in <a href="/wiki/Business_school" title="Business school">business</a> and <a href="/wiki/Management" title="Management">management</a>. Many state institutions have expanded their education scope and introduced new courses or departments. Institutions in Moscow, as well as the rest of post-Soviet Russia, have begun to offer new international certificates and postgraduate degrees, including the <a href="/wiki/Master_of_Business_Administration" title="Master of Business Administration">Master of Business Administration</a>. <a href="/wiki/Student_exchange_program" title="Student exchange program">Student exchange programs</a> with different (especially, <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a>) countries have also become widespread in Moscow's universities, while schools within the Russian capital also offer seminars, lectures and courses for corporate employees and businessmen.</p>
<p>Moscow is one of the largest science centers in Russia. The headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Russian Academy of Sciences">Russian Academy of Sciences</a> are located in Moscow as well as research and applied science institutions. The <a href="/wiki/Kurchatov_Institute" title="Kurchatov Institute">Kurchatov Institute</a>, Russia's leading research and development institution in the fields of nuclear energy, where the first <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_reactor" title="Nuclear reactor">nuclear reactor</a> in Europe was built, the <a href="/wiki/Landau_Institute_for_Theoretical_Physics" title="Landau Institute for Theoretical Physics">Landau Institute for Theoretical Physics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Theoretical_and_Experimental_Physics" title="Institute for Theoretical and Experimental Physics">Institute for Theoretical and Experimental Physics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Physical_Problems" title="Institute for Physical Problems">Kapitza Institute for Physical Problems</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steklov_Institute_of_Mathematics" title="Steklov Institute of Mathematics">Steklov Institute of Mathematics</a> are all situated in Moscow.</p>
<p>There are 452 libraries in the city, including 168 for children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mosru-stats_79-4"><a href="#cite_note-mosru-stats-79">[79]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Russian_State_Library" title="Russian State Library">Russian State Library</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> founded in 1862 is the national library of Russia. The library is home to over 275 km (171 mi) of shelves and 42 million items, including over 17 million books and serial volumes, 13 million journals, 350,000 music scores and sound records, and 150,000 maps, making it the largest library in Russia and one of the largest in the world. Items in 247 languages comprise 29% of the collection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p>
<p>The State Public Historical Library, founded in 1863, is the largest library specialising in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_history" title="Russian history">Russian history</a>. Its collection contains four million items in 112 languages (including 47 languages of the former USSR), mostly on Russian and world history, <a href="/wiki/Heraldry" title="Heraldry">heraldry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Numismatics" title="Numismatics">numismatics</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/History_of_science" title="History of science">history of science</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p>In regards to primary and secondary education, <a href="/wiki/Clifford_J._Levy" title="Clifford J. Levy">Clifford J. Levy</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> said "Moscow has some strong public schools, but the system as a whole is dispiriting, in part because it is being corroded by the corruption that is a post-Soviet scourge. Parents often pay bribes to get their children admitted to better public schools. There are additional payoffs for good grades."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Levy1_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-Levy1-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:1008px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">

</div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moscow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Moscow" title="Transportation in Moscow">Transportation in Moscow</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moscow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Airbus_A319-112,_CSA_-_Czech_Airlines_AN2166020.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="846" data-file-width="1158" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Airbus_A319-112%2C_CSA_-_Czech_Airlines_AN2166020.jpg/220px-Airbus_A319-112%2C_CSA_-_Czech_Airlines_AN2166020.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Airbus_A319-112%2C_CSA_-_Czech_Airlines_AN2166020.jpg/330px-Airbus_A319-112%2C_CSA_-_Czech_Airlines_AN2166020.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Airbus_A319-112%2C_CSA_-_Czech_Airlines_AN2166020.jpg/440px-Airbus_A319-112%2C_CSA_-_Czech_Airlines_AN2166020.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Airport,_Ramp_JP7551641.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="1200" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Airport%2C_Ramp_JP7551641.jpg/220px-Airport%2C_Ramp_JP7551641.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Airport%2C_Ramp_JP7551641.jpg/330px-Airport%2C_Ramp_JP7551641.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Airport%2C_Ramp_JP7551641.jpg/440px-Airport%2C_Ramp_JP7551641.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Airport,_Ramp_JP7551641.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Vnukovo_International_Airport" title="Vnukovo International Airport">Vnukovo International Airport</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There are five primary commercial airports serving Moscow:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sheremetyevo_International_Airport" title="Sheremetyevo International Airport">Sheremetyevo International Airport</a> (SVO)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Domodedovo_International_Airport" title="Domodedovo International Airport">Domodedovo International Airport</a> (DME)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Vnukovo_International_Airport" title="Vnukovo International Airport">Vnukovo International Airport</a> (VKO)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Zhukovsky_International_Airport" title="Zhukovsky International Airport">Zhukovsky International Airport</a> (ZIA)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ostafyevo_International_Airport" title="Ostafyevo International Airport">Ostafyevo International Airport</a> (OSF)</li>
</ul>
<p>Sheremetyevo International Airport is the most common entry point for foreign visitors, handling 60% of all international flights.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4airports_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-4airports-141">[141]</a></sup> It is also a home to all <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">SkyTeam</a> members, and the main hub for <a href="/wiki/Aeroflot" title="Aeroflot">Aeroflot</a>. (itself a member of SkyTeam.) Domodedovo International Airport is the leading airport in Russia in terms of passenger throughput, and is the primary gateway to long-haul domestic and CIS destinations and its international traffic rivals Sheremetyevo. Most of <a href="/wiki/Star_Alliance" title="Star Alliance">Star Alliance</a> members use Domodedovo as their international hub. Vnukovo International Airport handles flights of <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Airlines" title="Turkish Airlines">Turkish Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wizz_Air" title="Wizz Air">Wizz Air</a> and others. Ostafyevo International Airport caters primarily to business aviation.</p>
<p>Moscow's airports vary in distances from the MKAD beltway: Domodedovo is the farthest at 22 km (14 mi); Vnukovo is 11 km (7 mi); Sheremetyevo is 10 km (6 mi); and Ostafievo, the nearest, is about 8 kilometres (5.0 mi) from MKAD.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4airports_141-1"><a href="#cite_note-4airports-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are smaller airports close to Moscow, such as <a href="/wiki/Myachkovo_Airport" title="Myachkovo Airport">Myachkovo Airport</a>, intended for private aircraft, helicopters and charters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water">Water</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moscow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Water">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ilya_Repin_river_cruise_ship_with_North_river_station.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2326" data-file-width="3102" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Ilya_Repin_river_cruise_ship_with_North_river_station.jpg/220px-Ilya_Repin_river_cruise_ship_with_North_river_station.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Ilya_Repin_river_cruise_ship_with_North_river_station.jpg/330px-Ilya_Repin_river_cruise_ship_with_North_river_station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Ilya_Repin_river_cruise_ship_with_North_river_station.jpg/440px-Ilya_Repin_river_cruise_ship_with_North_river_station.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<p>Moscow has two passenger terminals, (<a href="/wiki/South_River_Terminal" title="South River Terminal">South River Terminal</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_River_Terminal" title="North River Terminal">North River Terminal</a> or Rechnoy vokzal), on the river and regular ship routes and cruises along the <a href="/wiki/Moskva_River" title="Moskva River">Moskva</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oka_River" title="Oka River">Oka</a> rivers, which are used mostly for entertainment. The <a href="/wiki/North_River_Terminal" title="North River Terminal">North River Terminal</a>, built in 1937, is the main hub for long-range river routes. There are three freight ports serving Moscow.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railway">Railway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moscow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Railway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3132" data-file-width="4776" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB.JPG/220px-%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB.JPG/330px-%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB.JPG/440px-%D0%9B%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B3%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B4%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3159" data-file-width="4737" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB.JPG/220px-%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB.JPG/330px-%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB.JPG/440px-%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%9A%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%BA%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BB.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kazansky_Rail_Terminal" title="Kazansky Rail Terminal">Kazansky Rail Terminal</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PaveletskayaSquare2016.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="682" data-file-width="1024" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/PaveletskayaSquare2016.jpg/220px-PaveletskayaSquare2016.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/PaveletskayaSquare2016.jpg/330px-PaveletskayaSquare2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/PaveletskayaSquare2016.jpg/440px-PaveletskayaSquare2016.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PaveletskayaSquare2016.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Moscow_Paveletskaya_railway_station" title="Moscow Paveletskaya railway station">Paveletskaya railway station</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Train stations to serve the city. Moscow's nine rail terminals (or <i>vokzals</i>)  are:</p>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belorussky_Rail_Terminal" title="Belorussky Rail Terminal">Belorussky Rail Terminal</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kazansky_Rail_Terminal" title="Kazansky Rail Terminal">Kazansky Rail Terminal</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kiyevsky_Rail_Terminal" title="Kiyevsky Rail Terminal">Kiyevsky Rail Terminal</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kursky_Rail_Terminal" title="Kursky Rail Terminal">Kursky Rail Terminal</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leningradsky_Rail_Terminal" title="Leningradsky Rail Terminal">Leningradsky Rail Terminal</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paveletsky_Rail_Terminal" title="Paveletsky Rail Terminal">Paveletsky Rail Terminal</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rizhsky_Rail_Terminal" title="Rizhsky Rail Terminal">Rizhsky Rail Terminal</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Savyolovsky_Rail_Terminal" title="Savyolovsky Rail Terminal">Savyolovsky Rail Terminal</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yaroslavsky_Rail_Terminal" title="Yaroslavsky Rail Terminal">Yaroslavsky Rail Terminal</a></li>
</ul>
<p>The terminals are located close to the city center, along the metro ringline 5 or close to it, and connect to a metroline to the centre of town. Each station handles trains from different parts of Europe and Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mostimestrain_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-mostimestrain-143">[143]</a></sup> There are many smaller railway stations in Moscow. As train tickets are cheap, they are the preferred mode of travelling for Russians, especially when departing to Saint Petersburg, Russia's second-largest city. Moscow is the western terminus of the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Siberian_Railway" title="Trans-Siberian Railway">Trans-Siberian Railway</a>, which traverses nearly 9,300 kilometres (5,800 mi) of Russian territory to <a href="/wiki/Vladivostok" title="Vladivostok">Vladivostok</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific</a> coast.</p>
<p>Suburbs and satellite cities are connected by commuter <a href="/wiki/Elektrichka" title="Elektrichka">elektrichka</a> (electric rail) network. Elektrichkas depart from each of these terminals to the nearby (up to 140 km or 87 mi) large railway stations.</p>
<p>During the 2010s, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moscow_Little_Ring_Railway" title="Moscow Little Ring Railway">Moscow (Little) Ring Railway</a> was converted to be used for frequent passenger service; it is fully integrated with Moscow Metro; the passenger service started on September 10, 2016. There is a connecting railway line on the North side of the town which connects Belorussky terminal with other railway lines. This is used by some suburban trains.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Greater_Ring_of_the_Moscow_Railway" title="Greater Ring of the Moscow Railway">Greater Ring of the Moscow Railway</a> forms a ring around the main part of Moscow.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metro_2">Metro</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moscow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Metro">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Metro" title="Moscow Metro">Moscow Metro</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_metro_map_en_sb.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1620" data-file-width="1270" height="281" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Moscow_metro_map_en_sb.svg/220px-Moscow_metro_map_en_sb.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Moscow_metro_map_en_sb.svg/330px-Moscow_metro_map_en_sb.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Moscow_metro_map_en_sb.svg/440px-Moscow_metro_map_en_sb.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moscow_metro_map_en_sb.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Moscow_Metro" title="Moscow Metro">Moscow Metro</a> route map</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Local transport includes the Moscow Metro, a <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">metro</a> system famous for its art, <a href="/wiki/Mural" title="Mural">murals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mosaic" title="Mosaic">mosaics</a>, and ornate <a href="/wiki/Chandelier" title="Chandelier">chandeliers</a>. When it first opened in 1935, the system had two lines. Today, the Moscow Metro comprises twelve lines, mostly underground with a total of 203 stations. The Metro is one of the deepest subway systems in the world; for instance the <a href="/wiki/Park_Pobedy_(Moscow_Metro)" title="Park Pobedy (Moscow Metro)">Park Pobedy</a> station, completed in 2003, at 84 metres (276 ft) underground, has the longest escalators in Europe. The Moscow Metro is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metro_systems_by_annual_passenger_rides" title="Metro systems by annual passenger rides">one of the world's busiest</a> metro systems, serving about ten million passengers daily. (300,000,000 people every month)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-metro_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-metro-144">[144]</a></sup> Facing serious transportation problems, Moscow has plans for expanding its Metro. In 2016 the authorities launched a new circle metro railway that contributed to solving transportation issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Moscow_Central_Circle">Moscow Central Circle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moscow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Moscow Central Circle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Central_Circle" title="Moscow Central Circle">Moscow Central Circle</a></div>
<p>Moscow Central Circle is a 54-kilometre-long (34 mi) <a href="/wiki/Urban_rail_transit" title="Urban rail transit">urban-metro railway</a> orbital line that encircles historical Moscow. It was built alongside of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moscow_Ring_Railway" title="Moscow Ring Railway">Little Ring of the Moscow Railways</a> and opened for passengers on 10 September 2016. The line is operated by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moscow_Government" title="Moscow Government">Moscow Government</a> owned company MKZD through the <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Metro" title="Moscow Metro">Moscow Metro</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Russia" title="Government of Russia">Federal Government</a> owned <a href="/wiki/Russian_Railways" title="Russian Railways">Russian Railways</a> selected as the operation subcontractor. The track infrastructure and most platforms are owned by Russian Railways, while most station buildings are owned by MKZD.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus_and_trolleybus">Bus and trolleybus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moscow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Bus and trolleybus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As Metro stations outside the city center are far apart in comparison to other cities, up to 4 kilometres (2.5 mi), a bus network radiates from each station to the surrounding residential zones. Moscow has a bus terminal for long-range and intercity passenger buses (<a href="/wiki/Moscow_Central_Bus_Terminal" title="Moscow Central Bus Terminal">Central Bus Terminal</a>) with daily turnover of about 25 thousand passengers serving about 40% of long-range bus routes in Moscow.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>Every major street in the city is served by at least one bus route. Many of these routes are doubled by a <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus" title="Trolleybus">trolleybus</a> route and have trolley wires over them.</p>
<p>With the total line length of almost 600 kilometres (370 miles) of single wire, 8 depots, 104 routes and 1740 vehicles, the Moscow trolleybus system is the <a href="/wiki/Trolleybus_usage_by_country" title="Trolleybus usage by country">largest in the world</a>. Opened on November 15, 1933 it is also the world's 6th oldest operating trolleybus system.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Monorail">Monorail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Moscow&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Monorail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Monorail" title="Moscow Monorail">Moscow Monorail</a></div>
<p>The Moscow Metro company operates a short <a href="/wiki/Moscow_Monorail" title="Moscow Monorail">monorail line</a>. The line connects <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timiryazevskaya_(Metro)" title="Timiryazevskaya (Metro)">Timiryazevskaya</a> metro station and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ulitsa_Sergeya_Eisensteina" title="Ulitsa Sergeya Eisensteina">Ulitsa Sergeya Eisensteina</a>, passing close to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/All-Russia_Exhibition_Centre" title="All-Russia Exhibition Centre">VVTs</a>. The line opened in 2004. No additional fare is needed (first metro-monorail transfer in 90 minutes does not charge).</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">
<div style="width: 155px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">
